Statistics of Chinese Goods Exported to the United States in June 167

All Items Decreased, according to the Continental Daily. Yesterday (the 13th), the U.S. Consulate General in Shanghai released the statistics of Chinese goods exported to the United States in June of this year, totaling US$1,588,721. The total value for the first half of this year is US$14,999,0159. However, this is only based on statistics from U.S. consular invoices. The value of goods subject to ad valorem duties by the U.S. Customs, which do not require an invoice, is not included. Analyzing the export value, inedible animals and their products rank first, including leather, feathers, ivory, pig bristles, etc., totaling US$501,736 in June and US$5,973,197 in the first half of the year. Textiles and their raw materials, which used to be the leading category, have fallen to second place, with a value of only US$437,953 in June and a total value of only US$3,156,113 in the first half of the year, indicating the decline in raw silk exports to the United States. Next are inedible plant products, such as medicinal materials, oilseeds, vegetable oils, dyes, etc., with a value of US$254,940 in June and US$2,633,194 in the first half of the year. Followed by metals, mineral sands, etc., with a value of US$144,835 in June and US$878,519 in the first half of the year. Next are edible animal products, such as poultry, livestock, fish, meat, eggs, etc., with a value of US$102,036 in June and US$659,405 in the first half of the year. Edible plant products are valued at US$81,275 in June and US$987,535 in the first half of the year. In addition, non-metallic minerals, such as glassware, ceramics, jade, etc., are valued at US$20,649 in June and US$115,124 in the first half of the year. Wood and paper are valued at US$16,243 in June and US$233,654 in the first half of the year. Chemical pharmaceuticals are valued at US$14,821 in June and US$76,208 in the first half of the year.

District Court Strictly Prohibits Extortion 168

Li Xianfu, a patrolman from the Fifth District, Third Precinct of the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, had a dispute with Shen Xiaodi, the deputy foreman of the No. 4 ferry of the Public Utilities Bureau, and sailor Hou Shouquan, over a mosquito net and pole being carried on the No. 4 ferry at the Ningguo Temple ferry terminal in this city on May 8 of this year, leading to a fight. The police from the Fifth District, Third Precinct, apprehended Li Xianfu and Hou Shouquan and sent them to the Nanshi District Court. The court summoned Shen Xiaodi for questioning on June 3. The Municipal Public Utilities Bureau also sent employee Li Mu to accompany him while awaiting questioning. After the questioning, the court ordered bail. Li Mu then went to the sales office to purchase stationery, but not knowing the format, he inquired with the staff in charge of the sales office. At this time, a shyster named Lu Xiang, who often hangs out in the Xinhua Garden teahouse next to the court, saw him, entered, and pulled Li Mu's coat to the Xinhua Garden teahouse, telling Li Mu that there was a way to deal with the stationery, but the timing was awkward. After Li Mu's request, he agreed to find a way for a price of three yuan. Li Mu explained that the bailee was an employee of the Public Utilities Bureau and that public funds could not be used at will. Another person then bargained it down to two yuan. Finally, for one yuan and two jiao, Lu wrote a bail bond from his own handkerchief package and sold it to Li Mu. Later, on the 14th of the same month, Hou Shouquan was summoned again and accompanied by Li Mu to the District Court to await questioning. After the questioning, the court ordered bail. Lu Xiang again sold a bail bond to Li Mu for one yuan and two jiao. After Li Mu returned to the bureau, he reported the situation to Bureau Chief Huang Baiqiao. Huang Baiqiao immediately sent a letter to the court's Chief Prosecutor, who was furious. He secretly sent a prosecutor to investigate the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau. According to Li Mu's confession, he knew the whole story. He secretly ordered Li Mu to turn Lu Xiang over to the court and ordered the staff in charge of the sales office to come to court to investigate. It was found that Lu Xiang, due to unemployment, had been borrowing the name of a lawyer in the Xinhua Garden teahouse on Xinhua Road next to the court, secretly making a lawyer's seal, selling stationery, writing pleadings for others, and reselling them to litigants at high prices, extorting money for a living. It was determined that Lu Xiang had violated Article 364, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law, and a public prosecution was filed according to law. The court hopes that the people in the jurisdiction will be informed. In the future, if they are deceived by shysters again and discover their exploitation and extortion, they should immediately bring them to the court with a guarantor and file a complaint. They will definitely be severely punished according to law.

In criminal cases involving major national and social interests, the court should decide to refer them to the jury for review. A petition to the Control Yuan to impeach Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng and Guan Yunhui for illegally extraditing Yun Huifang to the concession police station after she was arrested in the Chinese court's jurisdiction without submitting it to the Shanghai District Court for review according to law. Committee member Li Shirui was elected to draft the document, which will be submitted to the Standing Committee for review and issuance. (2) Standing Committee Member Shen Junru reported that the Association had previously donated 10,000 yuan to the Northeast Volunteer Army Support Association. Now, the Association has sent a letter stating that the Northeast military situation is urgent and that funds are urgently needed. Someone has purchased machinery for assistance. The procedure for allocating funds should be changed and funds should be allocated quickly. Resolution: Passed. (3) The Shanghai Second Special District Court's Secretariat sent a letter requesting that all members be informed that they should conscientiously perform their duties when assigned by the defendant to provide mandatory defense. If there are genuine obstacles, they should notify the Court as soon as possible. Resolution: Inform all members to pay attention. (4) Member Xu Yongyao's letter reported that lawyer Lu Qi committed perjury and requested review. Committee members Chen Tingrui and Zhang Zhengxue immediately declared abstention. Resolution: Forward the letter to member Lu Qi for reply. (5) The Shanghai Second Special District Court scheduled to burn toxic substances and sent a letter requesting that members be sent to supervise the event. Resolution: Committee member Zhang Zhengxue was elected to go to supervise the event when the time comes. (6) Lawyers Sun Zairen and Wang Shuchiao applied for membership. Resolution: Passed. (7) Committee member Shen Junru proposed to the Shanghai Second Special District Court to designate the first seat on the west side of the first courtroom (that is, the long seat opposite the police station lawyer's seat) as the seat for attending lawyers. Resolution: Suggest that the Second Special District Court discuss it. The meeting adjourned. A telegram to the Court and the Legislative Yuan reads: To President Ju of the Nanjing Judicial Yuan, Vice President, Minister of the Ministry of Justice, Vice Ministers Zheng and Shi, and President Shao of the Legislative Yuan and all committee members: Criminal jury trial is a common system in all countries in the world. Its advantage lies in enabling ordinary people to apply common sense and emotions to trials. The Association and legal circles in the country have advocated the adoption of this system for many years. Now that the country is in trouble, the patriotic actions of the people are not in line with the law, which is debatable. If everyone is punished according to the law, it will violate national sentiment and the national position, and it will not be using the court to speak for the enemy. It will make society and the public doubt the final result of the law. It is not established for the survival of the country and society, and if there is a danger of harming the country and society, if you want to talk about law and emotion, it is inevitable to get close to extrication. It is not only a population of real people to the outside world, but also a danger of destroying the law to the inside. The Association has carefully considered that in the case of such a contradiction between emotion and law, the jury system, which combines emotion and law, can be fair. Each time a criminal is caught, he is first sent to the jury meeting. If he is declared guilty, he will be punished according to law, and the people will have no complaints. If he is declared innocent, the dignity of the law will be intact, and the court will not bear the brunt, and foreigners will have no way to criticize. The adoption of the jury system in France is also motivated by specific facts. Now, such cases in our country are emerging one after another. The courts are in a dilemma, and society and the public and the defendants are unable to protect themselves. We can only ask your hospital to quickly formulate a jury system for national affairs crimes and issue it for implementation. All acts aimed at protecting the interests of the country and the nation who violate the criminal law, regardless of whether they are guilty or innocent, shall be handed over to the jury meeting for resolution, and then the court shall release them or declare punishment, which is the best way to plan. I hope you will adopt it resolutely. The country is very fortunate, the law is very fortunate. Shanghai Lawyers Association Standing Committee Shen Junru, Li Shirui, Lu Dingkui, kowtow, seal, cold.

Citizens' Association Presents Document to Municipal Government 172

Requesting the Promulgation of the Rent Exemption Situation in the Central District. The 21st Branch of the Shanghai Citizens' United Association and the Hangkou-Shanxi Roads Business Association stated that the Shanghai Municipal Government's announcement of four measures to reduce or exempt rent did not clearly specify the Central District. Members of the association often have lawsuits with landlords and cannot mediate. Yesterday, they presented a document to the Municipal Government, requesting it to comply with public opinion and promptly announce the details to avoid disputes. The original text is as follows: Presenting [to the] Petition to Promulgate a Clear Decree on Rent Exemption Measures in the Central District, to Ensure Fairness and Settle Disputes. It is humbly submitted that since the Japanese invasion of Shanghai on January 28, the entire city has united to resist the invasion. The public, under the rain of guns and snow, helped the old and the young, crying from hunger and cold, and fled to other places in an endless stream. Markets were closed, businesses were shut down, and the commercial sector was paralyzed. Japanese planes roamed and dropped bombs everywhere, day after day. At that time, the public was as distraught as if they had lost their parents upon hearing the sound of bombs. Victims were separated from their families. Alas, who has no parents, who has no wife and children? How can this situation be tolerated? The public lost their jobs and spent their savings. In these two months, no sector was spared from the losses. The scale of the losses is immeasurable. Newspapers have reported on it, and the facts are clear and undeniable. Although we have survived the disaster and reluctantly reopened for business, the devastation of commerce and the stagnation of the economy are due to the Japanese invasion. The enlightened people of Shanghai, in view of this, believe that if we do not take remedial measures immediately, we will not be able to relieve the public from their hardship. What is the solution? The first step is to demand the reduction or exemption of rent to ease the burden on the public. Therefore, various legal entities in the city have petitioned to determine a standard for the reduction or exemption of rent in the areas affected by the war, so as to relieve the public's distress and avoid disputes. Fortunately, the Municipal Government adopted it and announced four rent exemption measures in Announcement No. 28. However, the situation regarding rent exemption in our Central District has not been clearly promulgated, causing public anxiety. The Central District is also part of Shanghai and has the most prosperous businesses and the highest rents in the city. This time, it was also affected by the Japanese invasion. Japanese planes roamed the Central District, causing merchants and residents to panic. The streets were empty, and markets and businesses were closed. The losses were even greater than in the north. Even the cities of Nanjing and Hangzhou, which are adjacent to Shanghai, reduced rents due to the Shanghai Incident. Now that the government has announced rent exemption measures, it has remained silent on the Central District, as if the Central District is not part of Shanghai or there is some special relationship, and we are not given rent exemption, which is incomprehensible. Recently, because the Central District has not received any regulations on rent reduction, landlords and tenants have frequently had disputes and filed lawsuits against each other. Members have come to the association one after another, requesting assistance. The association is at a loss and has no way to mediate. Since the Shanghai Incident, various industries have closed to resist the invasion, and the Central District has also been closed for two months. At that time, the police were on high alert, as if facing a great enemy. Japanese planes bombed the city from the air, and the public were trapped and could not do business at all. The losses were immeasurable. According to the facts at that time, the rent in the Central District must be reduced or exempted in law and in reason. Therefore, we present the previous situation and submit this document to the government, requesting it to comply with public opinion and promptly announce the rent reduction measures in the Central District to avoid disputes and settle lawsuits. It is a matter of great benefit. (Omitted below)

Suspecting His Wife of Infidelity, He Actually Asked Doctors to Examine Her Twice 175

The Result Stated That She Was Indeed a Virgin Before Marriage

Song Tianxiang Still Abused His Wife

The Wife Could Not Bear It and Requested Mediation for Divorce

Song Tianxiang from Ningbo returned to his hometown in October of the previous year and married a fellow villager, Tu Fumei. Because Song practiced medicine in Shanghai, he took Tu to Shanghai a few days after the marriage. At this time, he suddenly accused his wife of not being a virgin and forcibly sent her to a doctor on Baike Road for examination. Ms. Tu had no relatives or friends in Shanghai and had to let Song do as he pleased. The examination determined that she was indeed a virgin before marriage. Song was speechless. However, after a few days, the suspicion remained. He sent Tu to a Japanese-run hospital on North Sichuan Road for a second examination. The result was the same as before. Song realized that he had insulted a woman and apologized to his wife with a whip. Tu wanted to maintain the marital relationship and was persuaded by her brother who came from Ningbo to Shanghai. They reconciled. However, after her brother left, Song's treatment of her became even more abusive. He secretly pawned her jewelry to fund his gambling and prostitution and neglected his legal wife. Although her mother-in-law came to mediate, it was impossible to reconcile. Recently, Tu could no longer bear to live with him and hired lawyer Wu Zhi to file a petition with the Civil Mediation Office of the First Special District Court, requesting mediation for divorce and compensation for all losses. The court approved the petition and ordered Song Tianxiang to appear in court for mediation.

Emergency Relief Report from the Shanghai General Office of the Red Swastika Society 176

After the Shanghai war, all the people were troubled by the difficulties, with tiles and rubble, and returned to their difficult livelihoods. Zhao, president of the Southeast General Office of the Shanghai Red Swastika Society, and Lin, Mr. Jin Jianguang, and Mr. Niu Zan, set off in June of this year, starting from Wusong to Jiangwan to Dachang. They lasted more than 50 days, and the disaster areas were the most serious in Wusong and Jiangwan. It is still possible to maintain at the Zhabei Baziqiao and other places, and no disaster relief is needed. All of the Wusong and Shanghai relief operations have ended yesterday. According to Zhao and others, the plight of the displaced people in the disaster area is unbearable to watch. The deaths in Jiangwan are estimated at more than 1,100, and in Wusong at more than 700. The survivors were all women, children, and the elderly. Although the purpose has been to help people get through their lives by Hongwanji's relief operations, there is still a long way to go. It is hoped that charitable organizations will find ways to take care of the aftermath, so that the survivors still have a chance to live. Otherwise, they will still be in danger of starvation. Total number of disaster-stricken households and the amount of relief funds distributed in the war zone: a total of 3,333 disaster-stricken households, with a total population of 12,899, and relief funds totaling 14,542 yuan.

Municipal Police Bureau Detective Team Captures Hu Lifu 181

The Arrest of a Traitor Can be Considered Punishing Foreign Aggression

Detective's Labor Alleviates New National Hatred

Since the outbreak of the January 28th Incident, half of Zhabei has been devastated by Japanese artillery fire, and the essence of Shanghai has been destroyed. All of us Chinese people should endure hardship and be determined to avenge the national humiliation. Unexpectedly, when our army retreated to the second line of defense, there were even madmen who betrayed their country and sided with the enemy, such as the traitors Hu Lifu, Chang Yuqing, Wang Du, Yao Zidu, etc. They seized the opportunity to collude with the Japanese, using the illegal organization called the Shanghai Beishi Local People's Maintenance Association as a cover. On one hand, they extorted money from the people, and on the other hand, they acted as spies for the Japanese army, providing the Japanese army with military advantages and harming our national army with military disadvantages. Their various crimes are countless. Among them, Hu was the mastermind. The municipal government had issued a warrant for his arrest. After the ceasefire agreement was signed, the traitors knew that they had nowhere to hide. They initially ordered their followers to spread rumors, saying that Hu had fled to Dalian and Shenyang, and some even said that they had fled to Japan, in order to deceive the arresting officers. In fact, Hu and others never left Shanghai, but their whereabouts were secret and unpredictable. They even disguised themselves and had close contacts with the Japanese. This was discovered by Lu Ying, the captain of the Municipal Police Bureau's Detective Team, who secretly ordered his subordinates to intensify their investigation a month ago, in order to arrest Hu and others as soon as possible, to punish the traitors and deter the wicked. At around 6 PM the day before yesterday, Captain Lu received a secret report from detective Hu Kui Sheng, saying that the traitor leader Hu Lifu was hiding under a false name at No. 198 Doulean Road in the Public Concession. Tonight (the 13th), he was scheduled to have dinner with his Japanese friend Yuan San at the Xinya Restaurant on North Sichuan Road. He requested that detectives be dispatched to arrest him as soon as possible. After receiving the report, Captain Lu immediately dispatched a large number of detectives to disguise themselves and wait at the address. That night, Hu was arrested. The details are as follows:

Disguised Reconnaissance 182

After receiving the report, Captain Lu immediately dispatched team leader Wu Xiufeng, along with detectives Chen Guangyan, Wu Zuorong, Liu Changrui, Wang Hongyi, Hu Kui Sheng, and translator Xia Zhongming, in cars, and drove straight to the vicinity of the Xinya Restaurant on North Sichuan Road, setting up an ambush. At the same time, Hu Kui Sheng, the informant, disguised himself as a waiter, waiting for Hu's arrival. At 6:45 PM, Hu finally arrived, wearing a straw hat and black glasses to avoid recognition. He was wearing a white summer cloth long gown and silk shoes. He first walked out of his residence on Doulean Road and walked to the home of Yuan San, a Japanese, in Yuqingfang on North Sichuan Road. Then he went to the Xinya Restaurant with Yuan San.

A Signal 183

Hu and Yuan San went upstairs to the Xinya Restaurant. Hu immediately took off his long gown, and the detective Hu Kui Sheng, disguised as a waiter, took the gown and hung it on the hook. At that time, the clock struck seven. Hu Kui Sheng gave a signal, and team leader Wu Xiufeng led the detectives upstairs, showed Hu the official document, and handcuffed Hu. A six-inch Browning pistol was found on his body, along with two clips of ammunition, a total of thirteen bullets. At that time, Hu's face was pale. He was taken to the car and directly to the team. Captain Lu personally interrogated him. According to his statement, he was 52 years old, from Wenzhou, Zhejiang, residing at No. 105 and a half Jinle Lane, Weihaiwei Road, Public Concession, and currently residing at No. 189 Doulean Road, where he runs a leather tanning factory. Since the outbreak of the January 28th Incident, he had no other actions. Until March 1st, after our army retreated, an old friend, a Japanese named Washizaki, invited him to the Zhabei war zone on March 24th to organize the Shanghai Beishi Local Citizen Maintenance Association. He did not agree at that time. Washizaki said that now in Zhabei, generally Jiangbei people are making it so that the local people cannot sleep peacefully, so they must find a way. He thought this was reasonable, and said to Washizaki that since this was the case, he must invite an upright Chinese person to maintain local order, and he would express his consent. However, if he were to do this, he would have to submit a request to the municipal government for approval before proceeding. Unexpectedly, when he was about to submit the request, he learned that the municipal government had already issued a warrant for his arrest, leaving him in a dilemma and at a loss. He had to organize the Shanghai Beishi Local Citizen Maintenance Association on Minli Road in Zhabei.

Confesses to Collecting Taxes 184

After it was established, it did cleaning the roads and burying dead bodies. As for the source of all expenses, it was to collect a tax of two percent of the estimated value of the goods when moving goods from shops in Zhabei that had not been affected by the disaster. Thus, it was possible to collect 100 to 200 yuan of transportation tax every day. At that time, due to the urgent work, he recruited dozens of plainclothes policemen and about a hundred investigators to investigate the moving of goods by various merchants, so as to estimate the value and collect the tax. The tax revenue was entirely used to maintain the local area. Therefore, when organizing the Maintenance Association, he did not ask the Japanese for advances. This matter was his own idea. Unexpectedly, while he was working, accomplices Chang Yuqing, Wang Du, Cheng Xizhi, Yao Wu (Yao Ziduan) and others under him did all sorts of disreputable things, resulting in negotiations. Later, the Japanese command forced the dissolution of the Association, and he fled to the second district of the Linping Road Maintenance Association. At that time, the general public shouted that they wanted to overthrow him. At that time, his finances were very tight.

Establishing Gambling Dens 185

Later, he discussed with Chang Yuqing, Yao Ziduan, and others to start a gambling den to solve the urgent problem. While they were planning, a Japanese named Yokota also had this idea. They went to discuss this matter, and he expressed his support. Cheng Xizhi went out to contact and recruit people to gamble, resulting in the opening of as many as eight places. Later, Huahui, opium dens, and native goods stores were all opened there. In a few dozen days, they obtained a total of 9,000 yuan in taxes, but the Japanese Yokota took more than half of it. The rest of the money was used for expenses. He requested an investigation into the facts stated. The interrogation ended at midnight. After obtaining the confession, Captain Lu, considering the importance of the case, ordered him to be detained in the team.

Captain Lu's Statement 186

He was sent to the detention center at 9:00 AM yesterday morning. Because it was Sunday, the office was closed. He will prepare a document today and transfer it to the Judicial Section for investigation according to law. According to Captain Lu, regarding the case of Hu and others, after the municipal government issued a warrant for their arrest, he actively investigated and never slackened. As for what a certain newspaper said today (yesterday) that Hu was fooled by the Japanese Yuan San and sold out his friends for money, it was purely fabricated. He instructed him to clarify this. He also said that after Hu was arrested that evening, considering the importance of the case and the need to pursue accomplices, a certain newspaper disclosed the information without consent, causing all the accomplices to flee, making the arrest difficult and dealing a blow to the detective's work, which was regrettable.

National Goods Association Asks Silver and Money Industries to Reduce Interest Rates 190

The Shanghai Citizens' National Goods Promotion Association believes that the silver and money industries treat loans to national goods factories the same as loans to foreign goods operators, and there is no preferential treatment for the industrial and commercial circles that promote national goods. It has been resolved to send a letter to the Silver and Money Association, notifying members to reduce interest rates, so as to comply with the intention of support. The original letter is as follows: "We hereby inform you that at the 26th meeting of the 12th session of our association, Executive Committee members Zhang Qingfa and Zhang Dexian proposed that the silver and money industries be asked to reduce the interest rates on loans to domestic goods factories and increase the interest rates on loans to foreign goods operators, so as to develop industry and alleviate people's livelihood. It was resolved to send a letter to the parties concerned for handling, so as to maintain domestic goods. It has been recorded that domestic goods factories have weak finances and rely on the assistance of your members for turnover. At this time of severe national crisis and the autumn of foreign goods dumping, it is an opportunity for domestic goods factories to step up production. However, due to capital relations, they cannot expand, and they can only borrow money for replenishment. We still hope that your association will notify all members, upholding the national spirit of protecting domestic goods and saving the country. In the future, the interest rates on borrowing money for domestic goods factories should be reduced by one or two points compared with borrowing money for foreign goods operations. That is, what is lost will be added to foreign goods merchants. There will be no loss to your members, and domestic goods factories will benefit greatly. This is also a way to encourage Chinese people to operate domestic goods and eliminate unscrupulous merchants who promote foreign goods. Economic aggression has a profound impact on the future. Corresponding letters are hereby sent, hoping that you will take note of this and look forward to a reply."

Son-in-law Stabs Mother-in-law Twelve Times in Anger 192

Wu Guangqin, extremely bored, Yangxingren, Baoshan. Wu Guangqin, 24 years old, used to run a gold business, but failed shortly thereafter, suffering huge losses, resulting in all his property over the years being used to compensate for the losses. Later, he was unemployed, so his livelihood was very difficult. Recently, he planned to sell the only two houses he had left in his hometown, so as to reinvest the proceeds and hope to revitalize his business. He once discussed this with his mother-in-law, Che Liu, while simultaneously planning to have his wife, Che Xingzhen, temporarily reside with her parents. However, he stopped because he did not get his mother-in-law's consent. Yesterday morning at ten o'clock, Wu went to resubmit his proposal. His mother-in-law, Che Liu, firmly opposed it, on the grounds that if the house was sold and Wu's business failed again, she would have nowhere to go. Therefore, they argued with each other and refused to give in. Wu Guangqin, in a moment of anger, stabbed Che Liu twelve times with a knife and fled. The injured parts of her body included four wounds on the face, three on the left arm, two on the left leg, and one on the chest. Later, neighbors noticed the incident. However, the murderer had already escaped, and they hurriedly hired a car to send her to the Hubao Long Hospital for treatment. It is said that the injuries were very serious and there was a risk of death.

Robber Commits Suicide by Shooting Himself 193

Bullet Enters Abdomen, Falls to the Ground. At 5:15 AM yesterday morning, four robbers suddenly came to the house of Wu Ma, a Wuxi woman, at No. 56 Glo Road in the French Concession. They were wearing white cloth short shirts and pants, of medium build, and spoke in the local accent. They entered through the back door and threatened with pistols. Two robbers stood guard downstairs, and two robbers went upstairs and rummaged through boxes and cabinets in the front room, robbing gold jewelry worth 557 yuan, wrapped it in a package, and escaped through the back door. One of the robbers, carrying the stolen goods, was walking north along Edward Road in the British Concession, when he was encountered by Chinese patrol officers No. 1653 and No. 1707 from the Laozha Police Station, who suspected his appearance and immediately stopped him, asking where the items came from. The robber replied that he had brought them from a friend. The two patrol officers saw that his answers were evasive and were about to take him to the police station. The robber saw that the situation was not good, that the matter had been exposed, and that he could not escape. In desperation, he took out a pistol and fired a shot into his left side. The bullet entered his abdomen, and he fell to the ground. The two patrol officers were shocked and immediately seized the pistol, notified the police station, and sent a car to take the robber to the Bureau of Works Hospital for treatment. The robber confessed that his surname was Qian, his name was Fu, he was from Wuxi, he was 26 years old, and he admitted the robbery. The patrol officers took him back to the police station to wait for verification.

Many Die of Epidemic 194

Died En Route. Zhou Shaoqing, 22 years old, from Taixing, used to work in an oil factory in Shanghai. Yesterday, he suddenly suffered from cholera with vomiting and diarrhea. His friends sent him to Nanshi, intending to send him back to his hometown. Unexpectedly, Zhou died after arriving in Nanshi. The patrol police glimpsed him, touched him, and found him still warm. He was sent to the Shanghai Hospital, where it was observed that he had been dead for a long time. He was placed in the morgue, and Qin Defang, the head of the 23rd district, was ordered to report to the District Court for inspection.

He touched him and found him dead. The deceased was about thirty years old, wearing a blue cloth short shirt and pants, and a white cloth shirt underneath. Lu Yongde, the head of the 16th district, reported to the District Court. The prosecutor and others arrived at the scene and verified that he had died of an epidemic. It was ordered that the Shantang provide a coffin for burial.

Unidentified Male Corpse. Yesterday morning, an unidentified male corpse also collapsed on Nanche Station Road. He was about twenty years old, wearing a white cloth short shirt and black cloth pants. Zhang Hongxun, the head of the 6th ward, reported to the District Court for coffin inspection. Yang Yin-shen Compiles "Outline Series of Chinese Literature" 199

Yang Yin-shen, in view of the fact that most of the Chinese literary history books published in Fangjian are only suitable for classroom lectures, and there are few supplementary materials available for students and teachers to refer to, has made a grand wish to collect supplementary materials for historical studies in addition to lecturing on Chinese literary history, and compile it into the "Outline Series of Chinese Literature". It consists of eight major sections, from ancient times to the Qing Dynasty, totaling 1.2 million words. All famous writers and famous works of the past dynasties are introduced and reviewed in detail, not only for reference but also as the largest Chinese literary history ever. The book is divided into eight volumes, listed as follows: (1) Outline of Chinese Pre-Qin Literature, (2) Outline of Chinese Literature of the Two Han Dynasties, (3) Outline of Chinese Literature of the Wei, Jin, Southern and Northern Dynasties, (4) Outline of Chinese Literature of the Tang Dynasty, (5) Outline of Chinese Literature of the Five Dynasties and the Two Song Dynasties, (6) Outline of Chinese Literature of the Liao, Jin, and Yuan Dynasties, (7) Outline of Chinese Literature of the Ming Dynasty, (8) Outline of Chinese Literature of the Qing Dynasty. The first volume, "Outline of Chinese Pre-Qin Literature," has already been printed and published by Huatong Bookstore. It contains 150,000 words and provides detailed descriptions of important pre-Qin literature, such as the Book of Songs and the Songs of Chu, each occupying 30,000 to 40,000 words. It also includes a chronology, index, and reference books for convenience, as well as many illustrations to enhance its beauty.

Random Notes

Cai E and Wang Jiang 207

— Zhanlu

Cai E, under the surveillance of Yuan Shikai, used a clever trick to escape. He deliberately indulged in wine and women, purposefully taking a concubine, and intentionally causing discord in his family. He even had a lawsuit with his wife, creating a plausible domestic squabble, so that his wife left in anger. Who knew that this was his plan to first send his family away so that he could show Yuan Shikai a clean pair of heels? Yuan Shikai, known for his cleverness, was ultimately fooled, leading to the cancellation of the imperial system and ending the political life of the Hongxian Emperor during his diabetic illness.

In fact, Cai E's trick was not original; it had been done before. He simply followed the original plan with some minor adjustments. During the Ming Dynasty, the exiled official and censor Wang Jiang was kept in Hangzhou by a Qing general who treated him as an honored guest with lavish accommodations. However, Wang Jiang's patriotic heart was eager to escape and join the supervising regent to restore the lost territory. He was only hindered by the Qing soldiers' surveillance, so he came up with the trick of escaping like a cicada shedding its skin. I read in the collected works of Quan Zuwang, a great Qing Dynasty writer from Zhexieshan, a passage about the censor Wang: "The official suddenly bought a concubine, whom he favored greatly. As a result, his wife quarreled and scolded him day and night. The official then sued her and had her removed. The wife also raised her arms and boarded a carriage, listing the official's hidden faults as she left, shocking the neighbors. The official traveled on the lake, and the guards, not suspecting anything because his concubine was there, did not prevent him from leaving. Only then did they realize that he had used a trick to get rid of his wife. After escaping, the official took his wife back and sailed to Jinmen to pay homage to the supervising regent."

Cai Songpo's trick had already been exposed in Quan Zuwang's collected works two hundred years earlier! It is said that there were many scholars around Yuan Shikai. If someone had shown the Hongxian Emperor this passage from Quan Zuwang's collected works while Cai E and his wife were playing this trick, Cai E might not have escaped! Why didn't anyone notice this article at the time? To say something outdated, it was fate!

On the Musician Liu Tianhua 208

— Jixiang

The famous musician Liu Tianhua passed away in the old capital a month ago. The news of his death was shocking. Everyone, both familiar and unfamiliar with him, was deeply grieved. Tianhua was the younger brother of Liu Fu (Bannong). Both brothers were famous figures in our hometown. After Tianhua's death, Liu Fu wrote on his portrait, saying that Tianhua had the deepest accomplishments in the pipa and erhu. The pipa piece "Ambush from Ten Sides" is majestic, powerful, and full of variations. It cannot be performed without Tianhua's great spirit. In the erhu, he was especially able to express his wonderful ideas and create new sounds. Every time he drew his bow, he could make the audience linger and savor the music, weep and sing for no reason, moving people deeply beyond compare. The erhu was originally a humble instrument, but because of Tianhua, it ascended to a higher level. Westerners who heard Tianhua's music exclaimed that without him, they would not have known that China had music. It is also said that in addition to his specialties, Tianhua also carefully studied everything related to music, such as the dulcimer, bugle, guqin ensemble music, as well as Kunqu opera, Beijing opera, Buddhist music, and popular music, and understood their principles and interests. He also had a glimpse of the study of harmony and composition, and the ancient theories of rhythm and temperament. He was also proficient in the violin and studied with the famous Russian teacher Tonov. Some say that he was the only person in the world who was proficient in both Chinese and Western music, mastered both theory and practice, and was able to understand the connections between them. However, he was always cautious and did not write easily. Therefore, he only wrote a dozen or so "Erhu and Pipa Scores" and a "Mei Lanfang Song Score," all of which have been published. His unpublished works include "Anci County Troupe Music Score" and "Buddhist Music Score," as well as several new erhu scores that have been completed or are still in progress, which will be organized and published by his disciples. These are all true records. And Tianhua's life was also spent on this. There are two musicians in our hometown who are equally famous in the world, one is Zheng Jinwen and the other is Liu. Therefore, I have a poem mourning him: "Two famous musicians in the world, Liu and Zheng are unparalleled. A generation of talents returns to the riverbank, the wind and waves move under their wrists. A song of 'Wild Geese Descending on the Sandbank,' how can we call it back by striking the beat before the tomb? The Guangling melody has no successor from now on, but there are cold tides sobbing for the deceased." Zheng Jinwen is proficient in ancient music and has hand-made dozens of ancient Chinese musical instruments, all of which are rare in the world today. Now that Tianhua is dead, only Zheng remains. Recalling the sages, I cannot help but feel emotional.

Random Notes on Taking Entrance Exams 209

— Ji

(1) When an admission test admission ticket falls into my hands, I am as happy as if I have already entered this university and become a Freshman. How troublesome it is to check my physical condition, fill out the application form, review my qualifications, and pay the registration fee. Now, I have overcome all these preliminary difficulties.

(2) It's almost twelve o'clock, I hurriedly hand in the paper and come out. The first thing I see is a few scribbled chalk characters on a black door:

"Car fare + dish money = registration fee." "Alas! The poor student is hungry! No food to eat!"

I suddenly remembered the physical examination fee, photo fee, registration fee, and car fare. I only got admission tickets for three universities and was squeezed out of fifteen big bucks!

(3) Xun said proudly that he went to take the exam for two universities and got seven more girlfriends, all very modern!

(4) Lian pointed to me, the one wearing a suit, he had met him when he went to take the Zhejiang University exam. Fei pointed to me, the woman with a white face, she was sitting in the seat next to him when he went to take the Shanghai University exam. Ah, I took a careful look at each face, and many of them seemed familiar to me. Wasn't it? Had I seen them in the examination room when I went to take the exams for those two universities?

(5) Only five minutes after the exam papers were handed out, a young man ran into the exam hall sweating profusely. He begged the proctor to allow him to participate in the exam, saying:

"Today is the last exam, I rushed thousands of miles from Yunnan to Shanghai to take the school exam, please let me finish the exam!"

"No, according to the rules, according to the regulations, it is not allowed to make exceptions!"

He had to leave with hot tears.

(6) In addition to writing a composition, a national university's Chinese language test also had two couplets: one was "Leaving home young, returning old," and the other was "Sun Wukong." According to the survey results, 80-90% of the people gave up on the first couplet. Mr. Chen, who usually has a lot of research on drama, answered "Achieving nothing, hair turning white." For the second question, most people wrote "Pigsy" or "Bull Demon King." Aren't these all Old Sun's enemies?

Gardens of the Capital 210

— Suicheng

The gardens of the capital, such as Drum Tower Park, Tao Garden, and Hu's Garden, are either barren and neglected or simple and narrow, and are not worth mentioning. Only the First Park on the bank of Fucheng Bridge, with its vast area and distance from the city center, uniquely enjoys tranquility and beauty. Therefore, garden visitors flock to it. To its south, the public sports field is only separated by a river. The river water is clear and the fish swim in groups. The banks are densely planted with weeping willows, creating a beautiful scene comparable to the Ten Mile Qinhuai River. In the park, there is a martyrs' shrine, a memorial tower, a library, a museum, as well as beautiful trees and flowers, and rare birds and animals. Everything that is needed to honor the martyrs, commemorate achievements, please the eyes and ears, and entertain the mind is fully available. There are many couplets by famous people in the Martyrs' Shrine, but they are all words of reverence for the martyrs and have nothing to do with garden visits. Only inside the main gate of the park is there a couplet engraved: "Come here to dispel all thoughts, but do not forget the revolution. Return and strive together, do not linger in this garden." The wording is moving, and the tone is neither soft nor harsh, just right. I love it very much.

The Central Party Headquarters is located east of Dingjiaqiao. It was originally the site of the provincial assembly. The trees are lush and the flowers are like brocade. In the past, it already had the beauty of a garden. Since it was changed to the Party Headquarters, the area has been expanded and developed, sparing no effort. Therefore, there are flowers blooming in all seasons, and trees that do not wither in the three winter months. The pond has fish, and the lotus pond has lotus flowers. The water and trees are bright and the scenery is beautiful. Even the First Park can hardly surpass it. Between the Secretariat of the Political Conference and the Statistics Office, there is a spring of water, winding like a belt. The lotus leaves are densely covering it. The banks are planted with poplars and willows, and the shade is dense. Walking in it, there is a long bridge across the water. The carved railings are extremely delicate and made of gray-white color, which reflects the green willows and red lotuses. Looking at it from a distance, it really has the appearance of "a long bridge lying on the waves, is it a dragon?" Such a beautiful scene is truly rare in the capital. It is a pity that it is the location of the agency, and the gate is heavily guarded, so outsiders have no way to visit.

Records of What I Saw and Heard in the Old Capital 銖菴 211

—

Crickets A tiny cricket can be worth tens of gold. Stored in a jar of clear pulp and fed with crab meat and chestnut yellow food. Treasure it and raise it and wait for the time to fight. Losing money and wasting time, all for the sake of a pecking game. It can be seen that the extravagance of the ten tribes in the old capital is not limited to sensual pleasures, pearls, and jade. The Emperor's Capital Scenery says that the fighting of crickets began in July. There are fields for fighting and owners of the fields. There are also teachers to raise them. Every family is equipped with fighting pots and jars. Then we know that this custom was even more prevalent in the previous Ming Dynasty than it is today.

In the old capital, those who raise crickets for fighting, in addition to children in the alleys, are all wealthy families. Also, according to what is called the teacher of raising them, it is what is now called the "Bashi" in the northern customs. These people live by insects. After the White Dew season, one often sees those carrying cages with red [blank] on Chang'an Road. They are all feeding the Bashi.

The Records of Yanjing Seasons says that the people of the north call crickets "Guoguor" and crickets "Qukuor". After May in the northern capital, there are Guoguors selling along the streets. Each one costs only one or two coins. By October, there are those who sell them in stalls. Each one can be worth thousands. In mid-July, there are Qukuors. The expensive ones can be worth several gold coins. There are white hemp heads, yellow hemp heads, crab cheeks, blue pipa wings, plum blossom wings, and bamboo joint whiskers. It is because they are able to fight. By October, each one is only worth several hundred coins. It is taken for its call only. The Qukuor also has oil gourds. During the autumn season, one coin can buy more than ten. By October, one can be worth thousands of coins. It is because its sound is clear and continuous. Listening to it on winter nights is both sad and happy. It is truly a leisurely person's elegant pastime. Therefore, the Qukuor cans in autumn are of Yongle official kiln, Zhao Ziyu, Danyuanzhuren, Jingxuanzhuren, red pulp, and white pulp. The best ones cost dozens of gold coins a pair. The ones with thick and solid bindings are the best. They are the so-called gourd utensils. According to the Nikka Kyubunkou, Hujia Village, five miles outside Yongdingmen, produces good fighting crickets that are better than those from other places. Crickets are born in the fall. Their sound is merchant-like and their nature is competitive. The people of today's capital can cultivate them. They keep their calls deep in winter. The method is to plant them in pots with real soil. The insects are born in the soil. In winter, the soil is placed on a warm kang. Water is sprinkled on it every day and covered with cotton. They lie dormant for five or six days. They wriggle on top. After another seven or eight days, they are like maggots. Place vegetable leaves. Sprinkle and cover them again. The feet and wings are formed. Gradually they turn black. They call within a month. They are thinner than in autumn. They rebel in spring. The other types of crickets include oil gourds, which are fat and oily, those with large heads are called Bangzitou, and those with sharp beaks are called Laomizui, and so on. In the past, playboy princes had nothing to do, so they indulged in this and threw away huge sums of money without hesitation. Now there are few who like this. Only children in the alleys sometimes use it as a game. Also, the Yanjing Miscellaneous Records says that there are grass insects in the capital. They are shaped like crickets, fat and green. They are born between summer and autumn. The sound of chirping is very noisy. Many people in the capital keep them in cages and wear them. The best ones cost more than ten gold coins each. The cage is made of a small gourd with the top cut off. Flowers and birds are carved around the four sides to allow air to pass through. The craftsmanship is exquisite. The price can be as high as a hundred gold coins. Many Eight Banner Manchu women hollow out the soles of their shoes to put them in, so that the sound corresponds to the shoes. If they walk or stroll, they look like they are picking flowers. This custom is almost abolished now.

Record of a Certain Policeman 212

— Hongliu

My Cantonese friend, Mr. Zheng, once told me that he had heard that in a certain county public security bureau in Zhejiang, there was a policeman who was very clever. He had only received a few years of elementary school education, but he was very literate and had a remarkable writing style. His calligraphy was especially beautiful. In his spare time, he would borrow rubbings of inscriptions and practice his writing. The director of the bureau was surprised by this and promoted him to patrol leader. The policeman was even more diligent. His calligraphy improved even more and he broadened his horizons. Gradually, people began to ask for his calligraphy. After a few years, he was promoted to clerk. He could write documents in an instant. The policeman's income gradually increased. He began to buy more famous rubbings. His calligraphy became uniquely self-reliant. His name also gradually became famous. All the famous scholars in the county sought him out. This was only five or six years after he first became a policeman. Later, he was implicated in the communist affair and fled. After a few years, he secretly returned to his hometown, but he was too poor to support himself. So he made a living by selling his calligraphy. His career was at its peak. He could earn sixty or seventy gold coins a month. His family of several people relied on it to survive. Mr. Zheng described it like this, and also said that he had seen his calligraphy, which was indeed handsome and extraordinary. A policeman like this can also be said to have talent and be able to strive for success in hardship. However, with his talent, if he had met a powerful person who could promote him, there is no doubt that he would have been able to enter the ranks of scholars. But he only became known for his calligraphy, and I feel sorry for him. However, there are already many talented people in the world who are buried. But someone like this policeman was still able to make a living by his art, which is not unfortunate. Alas, it can be passed on.

Financial News Last Week: Major Turmoil in the Gold Market 213

Rapid Storms and Utter Confusion

Once Approaching the 700 Taels Mark

Weekly High and Low Difference of Thirty-Nine and a Half Taels

Resulting in a Drop of Sixteen Taels and Seven Mace

Gold Transaction Volume Reached 23,000 Contracts

The Short Side in the Current Swap May Still Need to Pay Out

The past week saw violent fluctuations in the gold market. Ferocious waves ultimately proved impossible to suppress. The atmosphere within the market was exceptionally chaotic. Dealers were at a loss, bewildered and confused, advancing and retreating erratically. Daily fluctuations amounted to around ten taels. The momentum was unstoppable. Initially, overseas silver prices were reported to have fallen, but the large contracts unexpectedly rose, leading to a low opening at 741 taels and 3 mace. However, buyers were nimble. Moreover, due to the central bank absorbing cash, prices immediately surged, once reaching 48 taels and 5 mace. Subsequently, the silver market soared. The exchange rate loosened accordingly, with British gold exceeding one shilling and nine pence, and U.S. dollars also above thirty yuan. As gold prices repeatedly broke through multiple resistance levels, suffering heavy blows, the British and American exchange rates suddenly surged. It was rare for large contracts to experience such an astonishing surge. Consequently, a gloomy atmosphere pervaded the market, and sellers panicked. In the rapid storms, prices plummeted by over forty taels. On Thursday, the sudden drop brought prices to 709 taels. The following morning, the spot market even briefly crashed below the 700 tael mark (reaching 695 taels), which was truly unexpected. The bulls were greatly dismayed. Then, the silver market suddenly rebounded and contracted. Private telegrams and forward silver, along with exchange rates, continued to fall. Moreover, as the swap period approached, short sellers rushed to cover their positions, causing the market to turn from weak to strong, rebounding above 720 taels. The final settlement was 25 taels and 6 mace. Overall, compared to the previous Saturday, there was a further drop of 16 taels and 7 mace (a total drop of 22 taels and 3 mace over three weeks). The weekly high and low differential was 39 and a half taels, and the difference between the opening and closing prices was a drop of 15 taels and 7 mace. According to recent statistics, the total gold transaction volume was over 23,000 contracts, with short positions accounting for the majority, estimated at over 60 firms. However, Guangbang Hengxing made some covering purchases during the week, so its short position was relatively small, estimated at over 2,000 contracts. Furthermore, Dadecheng also had a short position of over 2,000 contracts. Zhaofengchang made successive covering purchases. The long side only accounted for over 20 firms, including major players like Mr. Wu, Jinyuanxingyong, Qianchangxiang, Yifengyong, and Runchangyu. Generally speaking, regarding future cash settlements, recently, red slips (receipts) initially added 8 taels and a half to the bid price. Later, due to the market price falling excessively, an additional 10 taels was added. As for the upcoming September/October swap, the short side may still need to pay out four or five taels. As for British and American silver prices, they have risen for three consecutive weeks, so the Shanghai market shilling repeatedly rose by one and a half notches (375), and the U.S. dollar by 625. Internally, the shilling also rose by 625, and the U.S. dollar by 8125 due to large exchange rate spreads. The gold firms initially sold and then bought back to offset previous short positions. However, the amount of short positions was estimated to reach four or five million yuan. As for exchange rates, both British and American rates have recovered by one point (reversing the small decline of the past two weeks). However, over six or seven days, the market seemed to be hovering without advancing. Yesterday (the 14th), the large contract silver price continued to be reported as falling. Today (the 15th), the gold market may still experience fluctuations. Moreover, dealers, as usual, privately engage in swap transactions one day early. Now observing the situation in the bond market, it is becoming increasingly chaotic, and its future is difficult to predict. Cotton Yarn News: Raw Yarn Greatly Boosted by American Cotton This Week 215

7,682 Bales of Spot Yarn Sold to Customers

In the cotton yarn market, the beginning of last week saw sluggish purchases from customers with actual needs. All traders lacked enthusiasm. Moreover, the war clouds in the Northeast were spreading, with the Japanese army invading Jehol. The situation remained severe. Furthermore, Japanese yarn flooded the market in the north, with particularly low prices. Local yarn was heavily impacted. All sales were seized by Japanese merchants. As a result, Chinese yarn had to be transported to Shanghai to find a way out. Consequently, morale was extremely low. Unexpectedly, on Tuesday, the American cotton government released estimates, indicating a reduction in production. The market price surged by 85 points per pound. World morale was greatly shaken. Raw cotton soared, leading to a corresponding rise in the closely related yarn market. It presented a sudden and rapid upward trend. Short sellers reluctantly covered their positions. Subsequently, on Thursday and Friday, the market atmosphere weakened again. Although American cotton rose, silver prices surged, causing the market to level out. However, major traders, seeing that domestic factories had depleted their stockpiles and that the overseas cotton market was unlikely to fall, were very keen to go long. Another group, due to many rumors, leaned towards short selling. The future of the yarn market lacked certainty. The prices for various months of raw yarn rose by 2.7 to 3.78 taels compared to the previous week. Total transactions for the entire week were estimated at 226,400 bales. Among customer traders, those from the south and Sichuan continued to purchase the most, estimated at 7,682 bales. Market prices rose by 2 to 3 taels compared to the previous week. Supplement to the Shanghai Shen Bao

Commentary

An Example of a Traitor 220

— Bu Fo

The notorious traitor Hu Lifu was used by the Japanese after the start of the Zhabei battle. In a moment of greed and blindness, he willingly became a traitor. When our army retreated to the second line of defense, he and his accomplices, Chang Yuqing, Feilong, Agen, and others, committed all sorts of evil deeds. The residents of Zhabei suffered greatly. Yesterday morning at 10 o'clock, a Japanese man named Hara San invited Hu to dinner, resulting in his arrest. What his crime is, the national law will naturally judge, so I don't need to say more.

However, according to Hu Lifu's confession, he has three sons, all of whom have noble professions. Now, due to his actions, they have all been dismissed from their jobs. He went to Xin Ya for dinner tonight, truly fooled by the Japanese Hara San, selling friends for money, and so on. But whether Hara San sold friends for money, I don't need to make a judgment before there is solid evidence. However, it is definitely true that his three sons, all of whom have noble professions, have been dismissed from their jobs because of his actions. As the saying goes, "One person's actions are one person's responsibility." If you become a traitor, the misfortune will not only affect yourself but also your descendants. If it is only a matter of a few bowls of rice, it is a small matter. Because Hu has already become a traitor, he naturally has the corresponding price of a traitor, so there is no need to worry too much. However, when others talk about it, it will always be "so-and-so's son, a traitor," "so-and-so's grandson, a traitor." This kind of loss of reputation is probably not just a matter of a few bowls of rice. This is an example of a traitor.

Pu Yi, Zheng Xiaoxu, and their ilk, with faces full of ambition, want to use the Japanese as a shield, dreaming their restoration dreams, talking at length about their history of using barbarians to control the Chinese, making excuses for their wrongdoing. Now, their beautiful dream should be waking up. Recently, the Japanese government also appointed Mutō to the position of Commander of the Kwantung Army. Political figures held a grand banquet for him. This move is completely to realize the unified plan of aggression. The good dreams of Pu Yi, Zheng Xiaoxu, and their ilk should wake up even more. But now, even if the good dreams wake up, it is too late. The title of traitor has already been put on, and no matter how much you use the water of the West River, you cannot wash it away. Even if you use scientific methods to wipe it, you cannot wipe it off. This is not enough to warn these few traitors. Their retribution is probably still to come. This is another example of a traitor.

But can such similar traitors be killed off, can they all die? I say, it is impossible to kill them all. Recently discovered traitors are like bamboo shoots after rain, flourishing. I have nothing else to say, only to ask them to pay attention and look at a few examples.

Literature and Art

The Lower Half of a Beauty 221

— Rang Shui

There are many who sing of the beauty, but from the waist down, they are all hidden and the wonderfulness is not conveyed, which is a great pity. The Book of Songs, Beifeng, "Gathering Feng, Gathering Fei," has no mention of the lower body. Therefore, based on the meaning of the Book of Songs, I have supplemented and sung of it, so as to avoid the criticism of "the small man is successful."

How can the hidden parts be painted? In front, a small figure stands on the empty steps, her embroidered shoes fresh. She removes the restraints and moves her steps stealthily. She lingers, loving the roundness of her six-inch feet. How can she allow the dew to come late at night? She truly desires to step on the waves and ascend to heaven. What can be done if Shen Lang is now thin and frail? Gently, for fear of pressing down on the shoulder of the poem.

I imagine her clothes cannot be depicted. Only explore the fragrant grass to the waist of her skirt. The half-body of flowers and dew hangs down. Along the way, the fragrant wind is tender with every step. The green trees are ruthless, blocking the shadow. The red pomegranate bows down, desiring to lose its soul. Why should the lower body be left out like the feng and the fei? Only by gaining a confidante can loneliness be comforted.

Oppressive Taxes 222

Science

What is Thunder? 223

— Bai Hong

During summer and autumn, thunder rumbles loudly. The powerful thunder and lightning a few days ago were deafening. This magnificent celestial phenomenon often causes fear in ordinary people.

What exactly is thunder? Where does the thunder in the sky come from? If you want to understand these things, we must first talk about electricity. The electricity in the sky is the same as the electricity used in our ground-level electric lights and trams. This was proven 180 years ago (i.e., 1752) by an American named Benjamin Franklin. He used a kite to draw electricity from the sky, causing lightning. This was a very dangerous experiment; a mistake could lead to being struck by lightning.

Now, what we need to know is: where does the electricity in the sky come from? Electricity comes from raindrops. Lightning and thunder only occur during rainstorms, as everyone can see. Before a thunderstorm, there is often a type of cloud in the sky, its bottom dark black, its top rising in jagged peaks, like mountains. Later, the cloud peaks suddenly collapse, and thunder rumbles. At this time, the updraft in the sky (i.e., air flowing upwards from the ground) is extremely strong. When raindrops fall from high altitudes, they are broken by this extremely strong updraft, turning back into fine water droplets and rising to form clouds. The clouds encounter cold at high altitudes and re-condense into large raindrops, which are then broken again by the updraft. In this way, after being repeated hundreds and thousands of times, the raindrops carry a large amount of positive electricity, while the air carrying negative electricity rises to the upper part of the clouds. Positive and negative electricity are continuously separated. Eventually, positive electricity accumulates more and more, and negative electricity accumulates more and more. At last, the force of attraction between them becomes extremely strong. When the air can no longer serve as insulation, that is, when the resistance of the air is limited and cannot resist the attractive force between the positive and negative electricity, then the positive and negative electricity break through the air separating them and make contact. At the point of contact, flashing electric light is emitted, commonly called lightning, and scientifically referred to as "lightning."

At the place where positive and negative electricity attract each other and cause discharge, a large amount of heat is released. At this time, the air in this part expands rapidly due to the large amount of heat and rises almost into a vacuum. Therefore, the surrounding cold air rushes into the vacuum with extremely great speed. Consequently, the collision of air with air produces a huge sound, which is the thunder we hear.

By the time the sound of thunder reaches our ears, the danger has already passed. This is because light travels faster than sound. Sound travels at an average speed of only 340 meters per second. If you count the time it takes to hear thunder after seeing lightning, you can calculate how far away the lightning is from your location.

Discharge between clouds in the sky is less dangerous. If discharge occurs between clouds and the ground, it is very dangerous, and people, animals, trees, and houses can be destroyed upon contact. During a heavy thunderstorm, it is best to avoid lightning by staying away from large trees, electric poles, and high walls. It is especially not advisable to stand in damp places or get completely wet, as these are all easy conductors of electricity and are very dangerous.

Casual Chat

An Afternoon at the City God Temple 224

— Kang Shi

The City God Temple... is a bustling area of Shanghai. Strangers visiting Shanghai always want to stroll around here and buy some things. If they don't, it seems like they've failed their mission to Shanghai. So the City God Temple is not only a place for strangers to visit but also a marketplace for Shanghainese!

On an afternoon when the scorching sun has subsided slightly, tourists, shoppers, and incense burners crowd together, replacing the air of the City God Temple with a tense, noisy atmosphere.

There are many shops selling foreign jadeite jewelry, which are promoters of foreign goods and, of course... the only good friends of modern women, aren't they? They are all surrounding the foreign jadeite jewelry shops!

Ding-dong, ding-dong... ringing continuously, suppressing all faint sounds and piercing people's eardrums. Ah! This is the peep show attracting customers! The Huxinting Teahouse... is one of the best scenic spots in the City God Temple. Turtles and fish under the Nine-Bend Bridge swim on the surface of the water, rippled by the cool breeze, occasionally raising their heads to breathe air, enticing people standing on the bridge to watch their naturalness and happiness. Unfortunately... a urinal has been set up next to the Huxinting Teahouse, and a foul smell is transmitted everywhere, like the stinky disinfectant used to prevent epidemics.

The Ten Kings of Hell! Constellations! City God! Everything, everything is filled with mystery. This is the unique art of our country, isn't it! "Sir! Madam! Would you like incense and candles?" Waves of annoying voices pass by the ears.

"Your complexion is very good! How old are you this year?..." When people walk to the fortune teller's place, they can always hear this kind of voice!
